commit 6fbd212a65c778d0befa600b70a9590449dae9f6
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Aug 8 10:35:33 2014 -0400

    Updated experimental.Division tests.
    
    Preparing Division for migration to mainline durationtools.
    
    This commit adds the following asserts to the Division constructor ...
    
        assert self.is_left_closed
        assert not self.is_left_open
    
    ... which are designed to enforce the idea that all divisions will be closed /
    open.
    
    MODEL: *ALL* timespans established by the gylphs of received notation in score
    are closed / open. We've known this for a while. The decision here is to
    enforce this fact on Division prior to migration to the mainline. This means
    that Division will no longer inherit from BoundedObject.
    
    A following commit will enforce the second half of this: all divisions will be
    right-open.

commit a9835da22562d18c3826fa8ace440cc9ed2fa6e1
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Aug 8 22:12:00 2014 -0400

    Extended TieSpecifier.tie_across_divisions. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    TieSpecifier implements two properties:
    
        * TieSpecifier.tie_across_divisions
        * TieSpecifier.tie_split_notes
    
    This commit concerns TieSpecifier.tie_across_divisions.
    
    OLD: TieSpecifier.tie_across_divisions could be set to either true or false.
    When true ties would be applied across the boundaries of all divisions. When
    false no ties would be applied across the boundaries of divisions. (The
    interpretation of the property was all or nothing, as the boolean implied.)
    
    NEW: TieSpecifier.tie_across_divisions can now be set to a tuple or list of
    boolean-equivalent values like [0, 1, 1] or [1, 0] or [0, 0, 1, 1, 1, 0, 1].
    The iterable of booleans is interpreted as a cyclic pattern showing which pairs
    of divisons should be tied (true-valued) or not tied (false-valued).
    
    See the EvenRunRhythmMaker API entry under 'tie_specifier' for a complete set
    of examples.

commit 9513e1e579982ae0af6315a92d2d5b7189cfdd6b
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Aug 9 11:03:00 2014 -0400

    Added TupletSpellingSpecifier to all rhythm-makers.
    
    OLD: only TupletRhythmMaker implemented a tuplet_spelling_specifier property.
    
    NEW: all rhythm-makers now inherit a tuplet_spelling_specifier property from
    the base RhythmMaker class.
    
    MODEL: the realization is that basically all rhythm-makers have the possibility
    of creating tuplets and so all rhythm-makers should afford a spelling interface
    for the composer. (Consider that NoteRhythmMaker happily generates a tuplet
    monda when passed a duration like 1/12 for example.)
    
    STATUS: the tuplet_spelling_specifier property is not yet integrated into the
    family of rhythm-makers. This commit serves only to add the property to the
    family of rhythm-makers.

commit 26de88f90c602146946c9e9578b10d0afcf27a4b
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Aug 10 20:16:01 2014 -0400

    Added 'preferred_denominator_from_divisions' property to TupletRhythmMaker.
    
    NEW FUNCTIONALITY: set the property to true to force tuplet ratio (where
    possible) to be expressed in terms of the numerators of input durations.
    
    The old default behavior is that tuplet ratios are always reduced and that
    the numerator and denominator of each tuplet are always relatively prime (thus
    making only ratios like 5:4 and 3:2 possible).
    
    With the new behavior turned on the numerator and denominator of each tuplet
    may not be relatively prime (thus making ratios like 10:8 and 6:4 possible).
    
    See the TupletRhythmMaker API entry for examples.

commit 329a491bfd6589bf5bab3c892217944d36c55aed
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 12 13:18:08 2014 -0400

    Extended Tempo.__div__().
    
    You can now divide tempo objects by numbers:
    
        >>> Tempo(Duration(1, 4), 60) / 2
        Tempo(duration=Duration(1, 4), units_per_minute=30)
    
    And you can still divide tempo objects by other tempo objects:
    
        >>> Tempo(Duration(1, 4), 60) / Tempo(Duration(1, 4), 45)
        Multiplier(4, 3)

commit f357c3e6b5ccb6931e8609a3844e9930071e49ef
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 12 14:56:49 2014 -0400

    Added Tempo 'markup' property. NEW.
    
    You can now use the markup=None keyword to cause a tempo to format as LilyPond
    markup.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> markup = Markup(r'\smaller \general-align #Y #DOWN \note-by-number #2 #0 #1 " = 67.5"')
        >>> tempo = Tempo(Duration(1, 4), 67.5, markup=markup)
        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 d'4 e'4 f'4")
        >>> score = Score([staff])
        >>> attach(tempo, staff)
        >>> show(score)
    
        >>> f(score)
        \new Score <<
            \new Staff {
                \tempo \markup {
                \smaller
                    \general-align
                        #Y
                        #DOWN
                        \note-by-number
                            #2
                            #0
                            #1
                " = 67.5"
                }
                c'4
                d'4
                e'4
                f'4
            }
        >>
    
    Note that this is the way LilyPond asks for unusual tempo indications (like
    floats or fractions) to be handled.

commit e71a8ea23cc14bb64e60332c48b15470d32e3030
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 13 14:51:51 2014 -0400

    Added Accelerando to indicatortools.
    
    Accelerandi format as LilyPond markup.
    
    Accelerandi are not followed by any type of dashed line or other spanner.
    
    Use accelerandi with a tempo spanner to generate dashed lines and other
    spanners.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 d' e' f'")
        >>> accelerando = indicatortools.Accelerando()
        >>> markup = Markup('foo')
        >>> attach(accelerando, staff[0])
        >>> print(format(staff))
        \new Staff {
            c'4 ^ \markup {
                \large
                    {
                        \italic
                            {
                                accel.
                            }
                    }
                }
            d'4
            e'4
            f'4
        }

                }

commit 03aa083ef7c361d85554b58629d57471899fe95d
Author: josiah-wolf-oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 13 20:23:34 2014 -0400

    Added `flatten` keyword argument to LogicalTieSelectorCallback. NOTE.
    
    NOTE: You can now choose whether to group selected logical ties by their
    originating expression, or to flatten them into a single selection.
    
    EXAMPLE: The following selector selects the first leaf of the first logical tie
    in every rest-delimited run of notes and chords:
    
        selector = selectortools.Selector()
    
        # select all leaves:
        selector = selector.by_leaves()
    
        # select runs of notes and chords:
        selector = selector.by_run((Note, Chord))
    
        # select logical ties, grouped by each run
        selector = selector.by_logical_tie(flatten=False)
    
        # select the first logical tie of each group
        selector = selector[0]
    
        # select the first leaf of each logical tie
        selector = selector[0]
    
    More concisely:
    
        selector=selectortools.Selector(
            ).by_leaves(
            ).by_run((Note, Chord)
            ).by_logical_tie(flatten=False
            )[0][0]

    name on TempoSpanner (and conceivably on all spanners that format in this new
    way).
    
    MODEL: we will eventually need a word for "indicators that do not contribute
    formatting but that are instead analyzed by a smart spanner".
    
    The use of 'annotation' in this commit kinda serves to do this. Even though we
    already have an Annotation class in the system.

commit fe1990fd6a41c457b336fd63e03d3bd2acc2d78f
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Aug 15 14:57:48 2014 -0400

    Taught MarkupCommand about the LilyPond \score markup command.
    
    Example. Here's the command:
    
        >>> small_staff = Staff("fs'16 gs'16 as'16 b'16")
        >>> small_staff.remove_commands.append('Clef_engraver')
        >>> small_staff.remove_commands.append('Time_signature_engraver')
        >>> set_(small_staff).font_size = -6
        >>> layout_block = lilypondfiletools.Block(name='layout')
        >>> layout_block.indent = 0
        >>> layout_block.ragged_right = True
        >>> command = markuptools.MarkupCommand(
        ...     'score',
        ...     [small_staff, layout_block],
        ...     )
    
    Here's the format:
    
        >>> f(command)
        \score
            {
                \new Staff \with {
                    \remove Clef_engraver
                    \remove Time_signature_engraver
                    fontSize = #-3
                } {
                    fs'16
                    gs'16
                    as'16
                    b'16
                }
                \layout {
                    indent = #0
                    ragged-right = ##t
                }
            }
    
    It seems somewhat incredible that this works.
    
    Extremely helpful.

        inspect_(leaf).get_leaf(0)
        inspect_(leaf).get_leaf(-1)
        ...

        inspect_(voice).get_leaf(-1)
        ...
    
    FUCTIONALITY: this now provides a one-line way of getting the first (or last)
    leaf in or from any component.

commit 936d88e2ab49161a55a2428f1ef6aa6177ca4aee
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Aug 18 16:27:25 2014 -0400

    Impelemented DurationSpellingSpecifier 'spell_metrically' property.
    
    The property is currently a stub.
    
    When set to true the specifier tells rhythm-makers to break each input division
    down according to the common practice understanding of meter. (So 3/4 and 6/8
    will be broken down in two different ways.)
    
    When set to false the specifier tells rhythm-makers to continue spelling
    durations with the fewest number of glyphs. (Old behavior.)
    
    Defaults to false.

commit 4b4920ea682f8e5f5ccc47a1b2e915e32113ee2c
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Aug 18 16:30:05 2014 -0400

    Taught RestRhythmMaker about 'spell_metrically' property.
    
    OLD:
    
        >>> maker = rhythmmakertools.RestRhythmMaker()
        >>> maker([(3, 4), (6, 8)])
        [Selection(Rest('r2.'),), Selection(Rest('r2.'),)]
    
    NEW:
    
        >>> maker = rhythmmakertools.RestRhythmMaker(
        ...
        Display all 286 possibilities? (y or n)
        ...
        ...     duration_spelling_specifier=rhythmmakertools.DurationSpellingSpecifier(
        ...         spell_metrically=True,
        ...     ),
        ... )
        >>> maker([(3, 4), (6, 8)])
        [Selection(Rest('r4'), Rest('r4'), Rest('r4')), Selection(Rest('r4.'), Rest('r4.'))]
    
    MODEL: this is the beginning of the process of teaching the rhythm-makers how
    (optionally) to notate according to common practice conventions of meter.

commit c690a2a60c8a13017878886514b1a560a4e36aee
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Aug 18 17:49:32 2014 -0400

    Extended DurationSpellingSpecifier spell_metrically with 'unassignable' option.
    
    You can now use ...
    
        duration_spelling_specifier=rhythmmakertools.DurationSpellingSpecifier(
            spell_metrically='unassignable',
        )
    
    ... to spell unassignable durations like 5/8 and 9/8 metrically (ie, broken
    down into parts) while leaving assignable durations like 3/8 and 4/8 in tact.
    
    NEW: note that this is a a very good approximation of common era practice for
    filling measures with rests.

commit 1c990d39f656b91f7f7ecd5a9a2501cc40219b57
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 19 10:41:13 2014 -0400

    Added markuptools.with_color() and markuptools.smaller(). MODEL.
    
    NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    These two functions alias the LilyPonds \with-color and \small markup commands.
    
    The contents of markuptools now looks like this:
    
        markuptools.Markup
        markuptools.MarkupCommand
        markuptools.MarkupInventory
        markuptools.MusicGlyph
    
        markuptools.combine_markup_commands()
        markuptools.make_big_centered_page_number_markup()
        markuptools.make_blank_line_markup()
        markuptools.make_centered_title_markup()
        markuptools.make_vertically_adjusted_composer_markup()
        markuptools.smaller()
        markuptools.with_color()
    
    MODEL: this is the tip of the iceberg of a new pattern entering the system. The
    logical conclusion of the pattern will be the addition of all LilyPond markup
    commands to the API. (There are a couple dozen such LilyPond commands.) The
    work of adding the remaining LilyPond commands will be tedious. But the
    benefits are striking.
    
    Compare:
    
    OLD:
    
        string = 'complicated string'
        color = schemetools.Scheme('blue')
        command = markuptools.MarkupCommand('with-color', color, string)
        command = markuptools.MarkupCommand('smaller', command)
        markup = Markup(contents=command)
    
    NEW:
    
        string = 'complicated string'
        markup = markuptools.with_color('blue', markup)
        markup = markuptools.smaller(markup)
    
    The benefits are fairly striking. Once the suite of LilyPond markup commands is
    implemented ...
    
        * we shouldn't have to initialize MarkupCommand by hand again
        * we shouldn't have to initialize any schemetools classes by hand again
        * we don't have to conclude every markup-manipulation transaction by
          wrapping a MarkupCommand in a Markup object
    
    Those benefits follow from the fact that new-style markup manipulation pass
    only markup objecdts around; other types of object are handled implicitly in
    the implementation of the different functions.

commit 9cdc934008fd70888bd0483d90a7177e437f61c2

commit 5c7778ff54b1a19a737767b4bb6f11d2ffd45be4
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 19 11:14:00 2014 -0400

    Added Selector TODO items. MODEL.
    
    Selector's inequality-related methods can be replaced in favor ...
    
        Selector.by_duration(duration=None, ...)
        Selector.by_length(length=None, ...)
    
    ... where the 'duration' and 'length' parameters are generalized to accept new
    DurationInequality and LengthInequality objects.
    
    The DurationInequality and LengthInequality classes don't exist yet.
    
    The DurationInequality and LengthInequality classes can be modeled on ...
    
        timespantools.SimpleInequality
        timespantools.CompoundInequality
    
    ... though those two classes should not be used as the literal base classes for
    the new DurationInequality and LengthInequality classes (because there's extra
    stuff in the timespan classes that's not appropriate for the two new classes).
    
    MODEL: this is basically a pattern of object-modeled inequalities. This is
    powerful for us. Because there are a number of functions and methods throughout
    the system the interfaces to which have always been less than perfect because
    the set of possible inequalities that might be used as restrictions in some
    operation is not bounded. (Note with Selector that it's more or less arbitrary
    that there are no Selector.greater_than_or_equal(),
    Selector.Selector.more_than_or_equal() and so on.) The solution is allow thin,
    core classes that allow the modeling of any inequality as an object that can be
    passed as input to other composite classes.

    OLD:

    ... is now awesome.
    
    MODEL: Markup chaining harmonizes with selector chaining.

commit e6efe47e04cab8949b405d7d20d4521b9a62ee12
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 19 15:42:01 2014 -0400

    Implemented Component._logical_measure_number. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    You can now call by hand ...
    
        >>> component._update_logical_measure_numbers()
    
    ... and all components everywhere in score will have their new
    _logical_measure_number property set correctly to a positive integer.
    
    NOTE: the functionality is currently private.
    
    CAVEAT: the update functionality doesn't work if you have multiple time
    signatures in effect at the same time (in different staves, say); the
    assumption is that all time signatures basicallys work at the score context.
    (We can generalize this later after baking in the existing version of the
    functionality.)
    
    Example:
    
        staff = Staff("c'4 d' e' f' g' a' b' c''")
        attach(TimeSignature((2, 4)), staff[0])
        attach(TimeSignature((3, 4)), staff[4])
        attach(TimeSignature((1, 4)), staff[7])
    
        staff._update_logical_measure_numbers()
        for note in staff:
            print(note, note._logical_measure_number)
        ...
        (Note("c'4"), 1)
        (Note("d'4"), 1)
        (Note("e'4"), 2)
        (Note("f'4"), 2)
        (Note("g'4"), 3)
        (Note("a'4"), 3)
        (Note("b'4"), 3)
        (Note("c''4"), 4)

commit b789e23c7065a4d7132b65d6f017894632bce1bc
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 19 17:33:30 2014 -0400

    Added Selector.by_logical_measure(). NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Examples score:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 d' e' f' g' a' b' c''")
        >>> attach(TimeSignature((2, 4)), staff[0])
        >>> attach(TimeSignature((3, 4)), staff[4])
        >>> attach(TimeSignature((1, 4)), staff[7])
    
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
                \time 2/4
                c'4
                d'4
                e'4
                f'4
                \time 3/4
                g'4
                a'4
                b'4
                \time 1/4
                c''4
        }
    
    Leaves in each measure:
    
        >>> selector = selectortools.Selector()
        >>> selector = selector.by_leaves()
        >>> selector = selector.by_logical_measure()
        >>> for selection in selector(staff): selection
        ...
        Selection(Note("c'4"), Note("d'4"))
        Selection(Note("e'4"), Note("f'4"))
        Selection(Note("g'4"), Note("a'4"), Note("b'4"))
        Selection(Note("c''4"),)
    
    First leaf in each measure:
    
        >>> selector = selector[0]
        >>> for selection in selector(staff): selection
        ...
        ContiguousSelection(Note("c'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("e'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("g'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("c''4"),)
    
    Last leaf in each measure:
    
        >>> selector = selectortools.Selector().by_leaves().by_logical_measure()[-1]
        >>> for selection in selector(staff): selection
        ...
        ContiguousSelection(Note("d'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("f'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("b'4"),)
        ContiguousSelection(Note("c''4"),)
    
    See the LogicalMeasureSelectorCallback API entry for more examples.

commit 73888b1f7f99ba7f8597b10e268c51778c8776a7
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 12:01:22 2014 -0400

    Improved makertools.DivisionMaker. GOTCHA.
    
    OLD:
    
        if self.remainder is Left:
            ...
        elif self.remainder is Right:
            ...
    
    NEW:
    
        if self.remainder == Left:
            ...
        elif self.remainder == Right:
            ...
    
    GOTCHA: using 'is' to compare Abjad ordinal constants fails after deepcopy.
    
    Here 'is' appears to work:
    
        >>> a = [Left]
        >>> b = [Left]
        >>> a[0] == b[0]
        True
        >>> a[0] is b[0]
        True
    
    But 'is' fails after deepcopy:
    
        >>> import copy
        >>> c = copy.deepcopy(b)
        >>> c
        [Left]
        >>> a[0] == c[0]
        True
        >>> a[0] is c[0]
        False
    
    NOTE that this same perilous behavior does NOT hold for built-in True and
    False:
    
        >>> a = [True]
        >>> b = [True]
        >>> c = copy.deepcopy(b)
        >>> a[0] == c[0]
        True
        >>> a[0] is c[0]
        True
    
    Might be possible to make Left, Right behave the same way as True, False by
    implementing Left.__copy__ and / or Left.__deepcopy__ carefully. But maybe
    better to just avoid 'is' comparison with Abjad ordinal constants altogether.

commit 610d5ef6d1c4d326cdfdf355785206415db43773
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 12:16:34 2014 -0400

    Beautified OrdinalConstant API entry.

commit 77f7cf95b5d8e1e7556b516d65148479bf236b75
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 20 12:34:13 2014 -0400

    Safety-proofed all ordinal constant comparisons with '==' instead of 'is'.
    
    Note that some experimentation showed that defining ...
    
        def __copy__(self, *args):
            return self
    
    ... on OrdinalConstant appears to "fix" the comparison discrepancies reported
    in an earlier commit.
    
    But it's almost certain that 'is' comparison will continue to fail after
    pickling.
    
    CONCLUSION: always use '==' (not 'is') to compare Abjad ordinal constants.
    (Just like for instances of all custom classes.)

commit 82633a285e1fa3ae8a2ca38121773c6e4e0e93e9
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Aug 25 10:19:09 2014 -0400

    Extended BurnishSpecifier. INPUT.
    
    OLD:
    
        >>> burnish_specifier = rhythmmakertools.BurnishSpecifier(
        ...     lefts=[Rest, Note],
        ...     left_lengths=[1],
        ...     )
    
    NEW:
    
        >>> burnish_specifier = rhythmmakertools.BurnishSpecifier(
        ...     lefts=[Rest, Note],
        ...     left_lengths=[1],
        ...     )
    
    You can now pass in classes (Note, Rest) as the arguments to
    BurnishSpecifier.lefts and BurnishSpecifier.rights.
    
    This makes the function of these two properties considerably more
    self-documenting.
    
    CHANGE: should be noted in the 2.16 release notes.
    
    Note that the old integer notation (with -1 for Rest and 1 for Note) still
    works. Though passing in classes is now the preferred way of configuring the
    class for reasons of documentation.

commit 7a86bfe0a3a724b3b30988f62c8bb3e064559122
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Aug 26 19:30:01 2014 -0400

    Added TaleaRhythmMaker.output_mask property. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Set like ...
    
        output_mask=[0, 0, 1]
    
    ... to a boolean vector.
    
    The rhythm-maker will then read the output mask cyclically as a final step in
    rhythmic creation. Each 0 encountered forces the output division to a rest.
    Each 1 encountered preserves the output division as-is.
    
    Useful for punching holes in rhythmic output in a patterned way.
    
    Note that it makes sense to implement this functionality on all rhythm-makers.
    
    This commit implements against only TaleaRhythmMaker.
    
    See the API entry for examples.

    NEW: TaleaRhythmMaker no longer ties rests created as a result of burnishing.

commit 08ff2e99bd3a336e5f50cc4be211b3649045f948
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 27 13:31:53 2014 -0400

    Added Meter.get_durations_at_depth().
    
    Examples:
    
        >>> meter = metertools.Meter((7, 4))
        >>> meter.get_durations_at_depth(0)
        [Duration(7, 4)]
    
        >>> meter.get_durations_at_depth(1)
        [Duration(3, 4), Duration(1, 2), Duration(1, 2)]
    
        >>> meter.get_durations_at_depth(2)
        [Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4)]
    
    Depths greater than 2 raise an exception because
    Meter.depthwise_offset_inventory is runs only to depth 2:
    
        >>> meter.get_durations_at_depth(3)
        Traceback (most recent call last):
        File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>
        File "/Users/trevorbaca/Documents/abjad/abjad/tools/metertools/Meter.py", line 1051, in get_durations_at_depth
            offsets = offset_inventory[depth]
        IndexError: tuple index out of range
    
    Method provides a semantic interface to meter duration, beat-group durations
    and beat durations (in that order).

commit 30c03b98d6e76dff63c2b1a7fe2f804221c69a8f
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 27 13:56:46 2014 -0400

    Added BeatDivisionMaker to makertools. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Example: beat-groups (ie, depth 1):
    
        >>> maker = makertools.BeatDivisionMaker(
        ...     depths=[1],
        ...     )
        >>> lists = maker([(7, 4), (6, 4)])
        >>> for list_ in lists:
        ...     list_
        [Division(3, 4), Division(2, 4), Division(2, 4)]
        [Division(3, 4), Division(3, 4)]
    
    Example: beats (ie, depth 2):
    
        >>> maker = makertools.BeatDivisionMaker(
        ...     depths=[2],
        ...     )
        >>> lists = maker([(7, 4), (6, 4)])
        >>> for list_ in lists:
        ...     list_
        [Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4)]
        [Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4)]
    
    Example: alternating time signature and beat groups (ie, depth 0 and 1):
    
        >>> maker = makertools.BeatDivisionMaker(
        ...     depths=[0, 1],
        ...     )
        >>> lists = maker([(7, 4), (6, 4), (5, 4), (4, 4)])
        >>> for list_ in lists:
        ...     list_
        [Division(7, 4)]
        [Division(3, 4), Division(3, 4)]
        [Division(5, 4)]
        [Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4), Division(1, 4)]

commit a56b5f71cee1cc98ab8e9176f59794742d6c2743
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Aug 27 14:23:57 2014 -0400

    Added RoundedRatioDivisionMaker to makertools.
    
    Example: makes output divisions with ratios equal to 2:1 of input divisions:
    
        >>> maker = makertools.RoundedRatioDivisionMaker(
        ...     ratios=[mathtools.Ratio(2, 1)],
        ...     )
        >>> lists = maker([(7, 4), (6, 4)])
        >>> for list_ in lists:
        ...     list_
        [Division(5, 4), Division(2, 4)]
        [Division(4, 4), Division(2, 4)]
    
    Example: makes output divisions with ratios equal alternately to 2:1 and 1:1:1
    of input divisions:
    
        >>> maker = makertools.RoundedRatioDivisionMaker(
        ...     ratios=[mathtools.Ratio(2, 1), mathtools.Ratio(1, 1, 1)],
        ...     )
        >>> lists = maker([(7, 4), (6, 4), (5, 4), (4, 4)])
        >>> for list_ in lists:
        ...     list_
        [Division(5, 4), Division(2, 4)]
        [Division(2, 4), Division(2, 4), Division(2, 4)]
        [Division(3, 4), Division(2, 4)]
        [Division(1, 4), Division(2, 4), Division(1, 4)]
    
    See the API entry for evne more examples.

commit 99c1ea24d4b3d2a78bb2020e4821b55102273d49
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Aug 29 18:13:53 2014 -0400

    Improved DurationSelectorCallback.
    
    DurationSelectorCallback.inequality now accepts a tuple of one or more of
    None, Exact, More or Less. This allows us to model model the concept of "select
    all components whose duration is greater or equal to x".
    
    The change is provisional until a proper DurationInequality class is
    implemented, after the current round of score are complete.

commit f03185ed6afbe46b08ff3c9c94ee3beb85c10032
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Aug 29 18:17:00 2014 -0400

    Improved formatting of pitched trills.
    
    Trill pitches command are now guaranteed to format after (and only after) any
    other command, markup or indicator which formats to the right of a leaf.
    
    This guarantees that markup is printed by LilyPond relative to the real leaf,
    rather than consumed by the dummy pitched trill note.

commit 72578e614913c228949f7fce1d908092d9e4cdba
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Aug 30 14:15:36 2014 -0400

    Added 'all packages - definition.py - illustrate' (di*) command.
    
    Use (g di*) to illustrate all segments.
    
    Candidacy protocol means that segments without changes will leave the
    filesystem as-is.
    
    NOTE: This means that you can run (di*) regularly as a type of scorewide test
    while working.
    
    Also good for ongoing scorewide tests are ...
    
        (s dt*)
        (s pt*)
        (g dc*)
        (g di*)
    
    ... and probably a few related commands.
    
    These are all designed to allow for frequent runs as proof that nothing has
    changed.

Date:   Sun Aug 31 20:54:17 2014 -0400

    Implemented Markup.__add__(). NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Example 1: markup + markup:
    
        >>> Markup('foo') + Markup('bar')
        Markup(contents=('foo', 'bar'))
    
    Example 2:
    
        >>> Markup('foo') + Markup.hspace(0.75)
        Markup(contents=('foo', MarkupCommand('hspace', 0.75)))
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.
    
    Should become the default way that composers combine markup and markup
    commands.

commit c2cb6ae73a02af4527fa27a7bdb68226961dd307
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Sep 1 17:38:03 2014 -0400

    Added ColorFingering to indicatortools. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Use for woodwing color variation fingerings.
    
    Produces scaled-down markup of a (positive integer) fingering number surrounded
    by a circle.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> note = Note("c'4")
        >>> fingering = indicatortools.ColorFingering(1)
        >>> attach(fingering, note)
        >>> f(note)
        c'4
                ^ \markup {
                        \scale
                                #'(0.75 . 0.75)
                                \override
                                        #'(circle-padding . 0.25)
                                        \circle
                                                \finger
                                                        1
                        }
    
    See the API entry for more examples.

commit 69baca996c199c8c9085ffa5813da5c34ef3384e
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Sep 2 23:18:46 2014 -0400

    Added NumberedPitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, fraction). NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Example: interpolates up from C4 to C5:
    
        >>> start_pitch = pitchtools.NumberedPitch(0)
        >>>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(0))
    
        NumberedPitch(0)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1, 4))
        NumberedPitch(3)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1, 2))
        NumberedPitch(6)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(3, 4))
        NumberedPitch(9)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1))
        NumberedPitch(12)
        >> stop_pitch = pitchtools.NumberedPitch(12)
    
    Example: interpolates down from C5 to C4:
    
        >>> start_pitch = pitchtools.NumberedPitch(12)
        >>>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(0))
    
        NumberedPitch(12)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1, 4))
        NumberedPitch(9)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1, 2))
        NumberedPitch(6)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(3, 4))
        NumberedPitch(3)
        >>> start_pitch.interpolate(stop_pitch, Fraction(1))
        NumberedPitch(0)
        >> stop_pitch = pitchtools.NumberedPitch(0)
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

commit 6619928d72ee696e2375844155a47e3c5b48fc4a
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Sep 3 15:43:44 2014 -0400

    Implemented Glissando.include_tied_leaves property.
    
    OLD: the Glissando spanner always included leaves in the middle of a logical
    tie. This is almost certainly not the behavior normally desired.
    
    NEW: the Glissando spanner now glisses into the first leaf in a logical tie and
    out of the last leaf of a logical tie (omitting leaves internal to a logical
    tie), by default. The old behavior is available by initializing a glissando
    with include_tied_leaves=True.
    
    See the Glissando API entry for examples.

    No public interface is currently implemented.

    to suppress LilyPond output.
    
    This can be useful when you want an instrument attached to score but you do not
    want the LilyPond instrumentName and shortInstrumentName settings to be written
    to output.
    
    Kind of the opposite of annotation.

commit 8824833f85a74c563ab9038f46628fa404034340
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Sep 6 17:13:05 2014 -0400

    Activated Markup.stack_priority property. NEW FUNCTIONALITY.
    
    Set the property to a (positive, negative or zero-valued) integer.
    
    The property is used at format time to arbitrate the order of same-directed
    markup attached to a single component.
    
    Example: foo higher than bar:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'8 d'8 e'8 f'8")
        >>> attach(Markup('foo', stack_priority=1000), staff[1])
        >>> attach(Markup('bar', stack_priority=0), staff[1])
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
                c'8
                d'8
                        - \markup {
                                \column
                                        {
                                                foo
                                                bar
                                        }
                                }
                e'8
                f'8
        }
    
    Example 2: bar higher than foo:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'8 d'8 e'8 f'8")
        >>> attach(Markup('foo', stack_priority=0), staff[1])
        >>> attach(Markup('bar', stack_priority=1000), staff[1])
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
                c'8
                d'8
                        - \markup {
                                \column
                                        {
                                                bar
                                                foo
                                        }
                                }
                e'8
                f'8
        }
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

    The files are named one per class.
    
    The purpose of each file is to ensure the autoeditability of a given class.
    
    It is conceivable that the directory could eventually house one file for each
    mainline class (as we work to make each mainline class autoeditable). This
    potentially large number of files is the reason for the separate directory
    committed here.
    
    It is also possible that in a later release of Abjad that these test files will
    migrate into the mainline and be housed with the classes they test, just like
    normal test files. But the reason for keeping these test files in the
    scoremanager branch is because they depend on the IDE. Mainline tests should
    not depend on the IDE. (At least not until the IDE becomes part of the
    mainline.)

commit c33b392ddd301840f03083c30b3d820337432cf2
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Sep 16 21:56:43 2014 -0400

    Changed public interface to mathtools.factors(). CHANGE.
    
    Function previously included 1.
    
    Function no longer includes 1.
    
    OLD:
    
        >>> for n in range(10, 20):
        ...   print(n, mathtools.factors(n))
        ...
        10 [1, 2, 5]
        11 [1, 11]
        12 [1, 2, 2, 3]
        13 [1, 13]
        14 [1, 2, 7]
        15 [1, 3, 5]
        16 [1, 2, 2, 2, 2]
        17 [1, 17]
        18 [1, 2, 3, 3]
        19 [1, 19]
    
    NEW:
    
        >>> for n in range(10, 20):
        ...   print(n, mathtools.factors(n))
        ...
        10 [2, 5]
        11 [11]
        12 [2, 2, 3]
        13 [13]
        14 [2, 7]
        15 [3, 5]
        16 [2, 2, 2, 2]
        17 [17]
        18 [2, 3, 3]
        19 [19]
    
    CHANGE: should be included in the 2.16 change log.

commit fca867d6516f254b78853bc67cc760f080e5f44a
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Sep 26 09:32:32 2014 -0400

    Removed experimental musicexpressiontools package.
    
    ASSESSMENT:
    
    musicexpressiontools constituted the most powerful staging area in the entire
    history of Abjad development. Ideas first implemented in musicexpressiontools
    included:
    
        * interpreter
        * score specifier
        * segment specifier (which became segment maker)
        * divisions (which became the output of division makers)
        * timespans (which migrated to mainline timespantools)
    
    These objects and ideas are now all central to working with Abjad in the most
    sophisticated way.
    
    Why is it possible to remove the many thousands of lines of code (and,
    especially, test artifacts) bundled together in the musicexpressiontools
    package? Some parts of the package were migrated months ago to the mainline for
    production use (timespantools, extensions to rhythmmakertools, experimental
    makertools, handlertools). And other parts of the musicexpressiontools package
    turned out not to be necessary after all, the most important case being the
    ScoreSpecifier and SegmentSpecifier classes: these are to be replaced by
    composers implementing their own SegmentMaker class(es) and using that class
    (or those classes) in the production environment established by the Abjad IDE.
    
    The proof points here were the scores that Josiah and I composed this summer
    (after two years of combined development on musicexpressiontools,
    timespantools, selectortools and the IDE): Krummzeit (in my case) and Zaira (in
    Josiah's case). The scores were assembled with unprecedented speed and
    formalized control. At the highest level the compositional process for both
    scores was the same: implement a custom SegmentMaker class, implement handler
    (or agent) classes to work as collaborator classes with the segment-maker; and
    then create a series of score segments defined in definition.py modules
    resident in segment packages (implemented one per score package), all according
    to the filesystem layout, import regime and build and test processes
    established by the IDE.
    
    This summer was, then, an applied test case to prove that extensive modeling
    done in musicexpressiontools over the course of more than two years was
    available in Abjad with the correct interfaces for production work.
    
    Was any functionality not ported over from musicexpressiontools? In fact, yes.
    The various affordances implemented in musicexpressiontools to select
    divisions, rhythms, components, settings and so on from not-yet-defined points
    in both the past and future of a score were never reimplemented in any explicit
    way in other packages in the system. This is ok, though, because a better best
    practice evolved in place of this: in the end we realized (unwittingly at
    first) that the classical inside-of-time / outside-of-time distinction due to
    Xenakis fixes these problems for us: the unlimited number of material packages
    allowed for by the IDE enable composers to generate arbitrary materials
    *outside of time* for inclusion anywhere in the score *inside of time* by means
    of a segment definition.py file. In other words, the knitting together of
    materials and their in-time positioning explicitly created by the interaction
    of IDE material package and segment packages removes the need for the look-back
    and look-ahead settings implemented in the now-removed musicexpressiontools.

    Added rhythmmakertools.mask_all() function.
    
    The function is an alias to make a boolean pattern that specifies that all
    elements should be masked.
    
    Useful when making, for example, a rest rhythm-maker:
    
        >>> mask = rhythmmakertools.mask_all()
        >>> maker = rhythmmakertools.NoteRhythmMaker(
        ...     output_masks=[mask],
        ...     )
    
    NEW: should be noted in the 2.16 release notes.

commit db9cd40e86b472297589170d92a8c18c61d62360
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Oct 11 15:12:21 2014 -0400

    Extended DurationInequality and LengthInequality to work with infinite values.
    
    This commit does several things:
    
    1. Extends DurationInequality and LengthInequality to work with infinite values
    (both positive and negative).
    
    2. Makes DurationInequality and LengthInequality empty-initializable. This
    means that both classes now implement keyword input parameters only. This also
    means that all parameterized tests now pass. (Several parameterized tests were
    failing previously.)
    
    3. Reverts DurationInequality and LegnthInequality storage format back to
    default. This works better now that both classes implement keyword input
    paramters only.
    
    NOTE: note the presence of these two classes:
    
        * timespantools.SimpleInequality
        * timespantools.CompoundInequality
    
    SimpleInequality is timespan-specific (and so probably not of any value to
    DurationInequality and LengthInequality).
    
    But CompoundInequality is a general object oriented way of bundling together an
    arbitrary number of (simple) inequalities together with the basic & | ^ logical
    operators. So CompoundInequality is probabaly of use when combined with
    DurationInequality and LengthInequality.
    
    That is, the final generalization of duration and length inequalities in
    selectortools is probabaly to be had by integrating CompoundInequality into
    the selectortools classes. Then we can say things like ...
    
        1/4 < duration and duration < 3/4
    
    ... and so on.

commit ba46fe629050a844fd35f4579a70729fd9fe8be4
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 21 10:12:37 2014 -0400

    Added rhythmmakertools.mask_none().
    
    The function is simple factory function.
    
    The function works in parallel to rhythmmakertools.mask_all().
    
    The function creates a BooleanPattern object equal to all zeros. (Compare with
    rhythmmakertools.mask_all() which creates a BooleanPattern object equal to all
    ones.)

commit 4b407ea1c7969aba9c5a00a5ef6289d2329becc4
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 21 18:23:33 2014 -0400

    Changed default twelve-tone row inversion. CHANGE.
    
    OLD: twelve-tone rows inverted pitch-classes around pitch-class 0.
    
    NEW: twelve-tone rows invert pitch-classes around first pitch-class in row.
    
    Explanation: the change accords with the historical way Schönberg and his
    circle inverted their rows.
    
    Note that there is now an axis=None keyword implement against
    TwelveToneRow.invert(). When axis=None the row inverts around the first
    pitch-class in row. To get the old behavior back set axis=0.

commit 4ae7555717c9fb48ffbdafdf5b1a25643012b79e
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 21 19:09:38 2014 -0700

    Implemented graphing protocol via __graph__() special method. MODEL.
    
    MODEL: This commit refactors the codebase to implement a graphing protocol
    analogous to the current illustration protocol.
    
    All classes which previously implemented a `graphviz_format` property or a
    `graphviz_graph` property now simply implement a `__graph__()` special method.
    This method returns a GraphvizGraph instance. The `topleveltools.graph()`
    function, like `show()` now looks for that method when attempting to generate a
    Graphviz graphh of an object.

commit 5457e9311f99fe73175dac8afe4f0a47d70157e3
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 28 10:22:12 2014 -0400

    Added new StaffPosition class to pitchtools. NEW.
    
    The class is an object oriented 'unit wrapper' similar to Duration, Multiplier
    and Octave.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> pitchtools.StaffPosition(-2)
        StaffPosition(number=-2)
    
    The class currently implements only a read-only 'number' property.
    
    The class will be integrated with ...
    
        * pitchtools.clef_and_staff_position_number_to_named_pitch()
        * pitchtools.named_pitch_and_clef_to_staff_position_number()
        * Clef.staff_position
    
    ... and so on.
    
    NEW: should be mentioned in the 2.16 release notes.

commit 85530e78840a1a7393e904d3c665afb8b53dff71
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Oct 28 10:46:21 2014 -0400

    Implemented Clef.named_pitch_to_staff_position().
    
    Example:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'8 d'8 e'8 f'8 g'8 a'8 b'8 c''8")
        >>> clef = Clef('treble')
        >>> for note in staff:
        ...     named_pitch = note.written_pitch
        ...     staff_position = clef.named_pitch_to_staff_position(named_pitch)
        ...     message = '{}\t{!s}'
        ...     message = message.format(named_pitch, staff_position)
        ...     print(message)
        c'      StaffPosition(-6)
        d'      StaffPosition(-5)
        e'      StaffPosition(-4)
        f'      StaffPosition(-3)
        g'      StaffPosition(-2)
        a'      StaffPosition(-1)
        b'      StaffPosition(0)
        c''     StaffPosition(1)
    
    Deprecated pitchtools.named_pitch_and_clef_to_staff_position_number().
    
    Use Clef.named_pitch_to_staff_position() instead.

commit 2882b227731f2c2b80cd4c2342f0dd28b9034624
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Oct 29 17:54:34 2014 -0400

    Implemented NamedPitch.from_staff_position(staff_position, clef=None). NEW.
    
    Removed ...
    
        NamedPitch.from_absolute_staff_position(staff_position)
        NamedPitch.from_clef_and_staff_position(staff_position)
    
    The new method generalizes the other two.
    
    Example 1: from absolute staff positions:
    
        >>> for n in range(-6, 6):
        ...     staff_position = pitchtools.StaffPosition(n)
        ...     pitch = NamedPitch.from_staff_position(staff_position)
        ...     message = '{!s}\t{}'.format(staff_position, pitch)
        ...     print(message)
        StaffPosition(-6)       d
        StaffPosition(-5)       e
        StaffPosition(-4)       f
        StaffPosition(-3)       g
        StaffPosition(-2)       a
        StaffPosition(-1)       b
        StaffPosition(0)        c'
        StaffPosition(1)        d'
        StaffPosition(2)        e'
        StaffPosition(3)        f'
        StaffPosition(4)        g'
        StaffPosition(5)        a'
    
    Example 2: from treble staff positions:
    
        >>> clef = Clef('treble')
        >>> for n in range(-6, 6):
        ...     staff_position = pitchtools.StaffPosition(n)
        ...     pitch = NamedPitch.from_staff_position(
        ...         staff_position,
        ...         clef=clef,
        ...         )
        ...     message = '{!s}\t{}'.format(staff_position, pitch)
        ...     print(message)
        StaffPosition(-6)       c'
        StaffPosition(-5)       d'
        StaffPosition(-4)       e'
        StaffPosition(-3)       f'
        StaffPosition(-2)       g'
        StaffPosition(-1)       a'
        StaffPosition(0)        b'
        StaffPosition(1)        c''
        StaffPosition(2)        d''
        StaffPosition(3)        e''
        StaffPosition(4)        f''
        StaffPosition(5)        g''
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

commit b065d82bad5b17b762f32fe51e7ba24e1f66b850
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Oct 30 14:03:56 2014 -0700

    Added scoretools.DrumNoteHead. NOTE.
    
    NOTE. You can now create "drum" notes for use in a DrumStaff context.
    
    The LilyPondParser will attempt to parse valid drum pitches ('snare', 'tamb',
    'bd' etc) into DrumNoteHeads. Additionally, Chord and Note now accept
    DrumNoteHead instances in place of NoteHeads.
    
    To create drum music, use the following recipe:
    
        drums = Container('hihat4 hh bassdrum bd')
        drum_mode = indicatortools.LilyPondCommand(
            'drummode',
            format_slot='before',
            )
        attach(drum_mode, drums)
        drum_staff = Staff(
            music=[drums],
            context_name='DrumStaff',
            )
    
    The results in a properly constructed piece of drum music:
    
        >>> f(drum_staff)
        \new DrumStaff {
                \drummode
                {
                        hihat4
                        hihat4
                        bassdrum4
                        bassdrum4
                }
        }

commit ee430ef701aea7bee9cdfab20040cb5ff255b8b4
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Sat Nov 8 14:09:32 2014 -0800

    Improved Duration instantiation.
    
    You can now properly instantiate a duration from an object which *has* a
    duration.
    
    Previously, incorrectly:
    
        >>> time_signature = TimeSignature(3, 4)
        >>> Duration(time_signature)
        Duration(3, 1)
    
    Now, correctly:
    
        >>> time_signature = TimeSignature(3, 4)
        >>> Duration(time_signature)
        Duration(3, 4)

commit 2023ae495d09ca874a566f50140073cde9b6110a
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Dec 4 10:20:26 2014 -0800

    Timer now takes an optional "message" argument.
    
    On __exit__, if "message" is not None, Timer will print its message and elapsed
    time. This simplifies the Timer idiom:
    
        with systemtools.Timer() as timer:
            print('PitchHandler:')
            consort.PitchHandler._process_session(
                segment_session,
                )
        print('\ttotal:', timer.elapsed_time)
    
    ... becomes...
    
        with systemtools.Timer('\ttotal'):
            print('PitchHandler:')
            consort.PitchHandler._process_session(
                segment_session,
                )

commit 678f943db012f38ef0d95aec8a36222ab5867e8d
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 9 12:05:28 2014 -0500

    Added new Transition class to indicatortools.
    
    The class is current a stub.
    
    The class encapsulate the graphic properties of the line-drawn part of text
    spanners: line dashing, endpoint padding, endpoint arrows and so on.
    
    This new Transition class will be used together with the existing Markup and
    TextSpanner classes to afford multistage text spanner definition in a piecewise
    way.

    OLD: Spanner._leaves
    NEW: Spanner._get_leaves()
    
    Explanation: the code involves (potentially extensive) iteration. The old
    implementation as a property conceals the fact that the call could be costly.
    The new implementation as a method avoids this.

commit c7005a1c550726ef13ab8533c2a5772ffc30fa5d
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Dec 10 13:53:21 2014 -0500

    Added new Arrow class to indicatortools. NEW.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 d'4 e'4 f'4")
        >>> start_markup = Markup('pont.').upright()
        >>> stop_markup = Markup('ord.').upright()
        >>> arrow = indicatortools.Arrow()
    
        >>> attach(start_markup, staff[0], is_annotation=True)
        >>> attach(stop_markup, staff[-1], is_annotation=True)
        >>> attach(arrow, staff[0])
        >>> attach(spannertools.TextSpanner(), staff[:])
    
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
                \once \override TextSpanner.arrow-width = 0.25
                \once \override TextSpanner.bound-details.left.stencil-align-dir-y = 0
                \once \override TextSpanner.bound-details.left.text = \markup {
                        \concat
                                {
                                        \upright
                                                pont.
                                        \hspace
                                                #0.25
                                }
                        }
                \once \override TextSpanner.bound-details.right.arrow = ##t
                \once \override TextSpanner.bound-details.right.padding = 1.5
                \once \override TextSpanner.bound-details.right.stencil-align-dir-y = 0
                \once \override TextSpanner.dash-fraction = 1
                c'4 \startTextSpan
                d'4
                e'4
                f'4 \stopTextSpan ^ \markup {
                        \upright
                                ord.
                        }
        }
    
    See the arrow API entry for notation.
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

    NEW: Glissando includes repeated pitches when include_repeated_pitches=True.
    Glissando excludes repeated pitches when include_repeated_pitches=False.
    
    Glissando now defaults to include_repeated_pitches=False.
    
    Set include_repeated_pitches=True to recoup the old behavior.
    
    Doesn't need to be included in the change log.

commit 41459968c4210ce290bcf5154069fdb15f5596df
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Dec 15 19:40:28 2014 -0800

    Added Selector.with_callback() method. MODEL.
    
    MODEL: Selector.with_callback() lets composers create selectors with arbitrary
    callbacks. Many callbacks which might be useful during the component selection
    process are also likely very composition-specific. You can now simply create
    selector callbacks in your makers subpackage and configure selectors with them
    directly.
    
    For example, a composer might wish to partition a sequence of leaves into
    subsequences where each subsequence's last leaf has an after-grace container
    attached. This functionality is probably too eccentric for inclusion in Abjad,
    but should be facilitated nonetheless. Just create a SelectorCallback which
    encapsulates this partitioning logic and aggregate it into a Selector via
    Selector.with_callback().

commit c1cc05e4144ef57324f1f1f53788cbf669a9c435
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Dec 29 16:26:41 2014 -0500

    Added Tremolo to indicatortools.
    
    The class is currently a stub.
    
    After implementation the class will be used like this:
    
        >>> chord = Chord("<c d>1")
        >>> tremolo = indicatortools.Tremolo(beam_count=2)
        >>> attach(tremolo, chord)
        >>> f(chord)
        \repeat tremolo 8 { c16 d }
    
    This means that attaching a tremolo indicator to a chord will cause the chord
    to behave differently at format time.
    
    Attaching a tremolo to a note or rest will have no effect.

commit bbe0a322e7d0ff459058f9a4d5655bc3503383b0
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 30 12:54:40 2014 -0500

    Extended Tremolo with 'is_slurred' property.
    
    Set to true to slur tremolo:
    
        >>> chord = Chord("<cs' e'>4")
        >>> tremolo = indicatortools.Tremolo(is_slurred=True)
        >>> attach(tremolo, chord)
    
        >>> f(chord)
        \repeat tremolo 4
        {
        cs'32 \( e'32 \)
        }
    
    This is the correct notation for fingered tremolo on bowed string instruments.
    
    Defaults to false.

commit eb0e9eccc5128b53353bfbbc7288374dfb4ce51d
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 30 19:17:53 2014 -0800

    Extended CountsSelectorCallback. NOTE.
    
    You can now use negative counts. They will be treated as positive for the
    purposes of partitioning selections, but the partitioned parts associated with
    the negative counts will not be included in the result.
    
    This is useful for creating selected and un-selected runs of leaves:
    
        selectortools.Selector(
            ).by_leaves(
            ).by_counts(
                [-7, 2, -3, 1],
                )

commit 917d332c1f936a2c3952dc3343d22f5152d50340
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Dec 30 19:21:07 2014 -0800

    Extended CountsSelectorCallback.
    
    You can now use negative counts. They will be treated as positive for the
    purposes of partitioning selections, but the partitioned parts associated with
    the negative counts will not be included in the result.
    
    This is useful for creating selected and un-selected runs of leaves. The
    following selector will skip 7 leaves, select 2, skip 3, then select 1:
    
        selectortools.Selector(
            ).by_leaves(
            ).by_counts(
                [-7, 2, -3, 1],
                )

commit 0ada8059ad7eb2615c1f18964b64f740ae9f1d5f
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Jan 2 22:35:21 2015 -0800

    Improved LilyPondFormatManager.
    
    When formatting non-scoped indicators, LilyPondFormatManager will attempt to
    find and use the indicator's `_get_lilypond_format_bundle()` method before it
    tries to get a bundle via the indicator's `_lilypond_format_bundle` property.
    
    The method `_get_lilypond_format_bundle()` is conceptually identical to the
    identically named method on `Spanner`. It allows for providing format
    contributions conditionally based on the component to which the indicator is
    attached.

commit c34357cf633f003fdbf6ade5df1c309030a39208
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 4 19:42:35 2015 -0500

    Cleaned up TextSpanner API entry.

commit 84f1a98d97d0894b0aa3fb2047c20e570ea5c4b9
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 4 19:59:15 2015 -0500

    Fixed interaction between TextSpanner and annotated markup.
    
    Consider this example:
    
        staff = Staff("c'4 d'4 e'4 f'4")
        markup = Markup('foo')
        attach(markup, staff[0], is_annotation=True)
        attach(spannertools.TextSpanner(), staff[:])
    
    OLD OUTPUT:
    
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
            c'4 ^ \markup { foo }
            d'4
            e'4
            f'4 \stopTextSpan
        }
    
    NEW OUTPUT:
    
        >>> f(staff)
        \new Staff {
            c'4 ^ \markup { foo }
            d'4
            e'4
            f'4
        }
    
    Explanation: First note that 'annotated markup' means markup attached to a
    component with is_annotation=True set in the call to attach(). Then note that
    2.16 greatly extends the behavior of TextSpanner (which should be included in
    the 2.16 release notes). TextSpanner now interacts with annotated markup in
    intelligent ways. It remains to document the complete set of new behaviors that
    determine the ways that TextSpanner interacts with annotated markup. But
    suffice it to say for this commit that TextSpanner now knows about annotated
    markup and also about the new LineSegment and Arrow classes. When
    TextSpanner find Markup, LineSegment or Arrow objects attached to leaves,
    TextSpanner formats all of these objects together in an intelligent way. This
    sort of group formatting sometimes includes silencing the \startTextSpan and
    \stopTextSpan commands that are the usual output of TextSpanner. The bug fixed
    in this commit causes a spurious \stopTextSpan to no longer appear.

commit ec82949e996a0fc1472334e538787e1e80570d36
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Jan 4 20:04:10 2015 -0800

    Streamlined LilyPond formatting.
    
    Explanation: all instances of a "_lilypond_format_bundle" read-only property
    have been replaced by a "_get_lilypond_format_bundle(component)" method. This
    brings indicator formatting closer in-line with spanner formatting.
    
    Ultimately, all non-component formatting contributions for spanners and
    indicators should be contributed via an identical interface. Once this is
    established, we can expand the "_get_lilypond_format_bundle(...)" argument
    signature to accept not only a component, but also an optional formatting memo.
    This will let us do things like cache information used by spanners (the leaves
    in the spanner, any relevant annotations attached to those leaves) for faster
    formatting times.

commit f1b94a056131496070209a026a4e659d08808204
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 27 14:17:45 2015 -0800

    Improved docstrings in LilyPondFile. NOTE.
    
    NOTE: When writing loops or other nested blocks in docstrings, please make sure
    to include the final "blank" line, as though you were typing the docstring in
    at the interpreter.
    
    While doctesting will treat the following as valid:
    
        >>> for blah in bloo:
        ...     print(blah)
        'wee'
        'woo'
    
    ... it looks like a malformed intepreter session.
    
    Instead, format the example like this:
    
        >>> for blah in bloo:
        ...     print(blah)
        ...
        'wee'
        'woo'

commit 41d869682cf107fb1080987add98a6f6c8fab946
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Jan 27 14:20:46 2015 -0800

    Added TemporaryDirectory context manager to systemtools.
    
    Use this context manager to create, return and then destroy a temporary
    directory:
    
        with systemtools.TemporaryDirectory() as temp_directory:
            temp_file = os.path.join(temp_directory, 'foo.txt'):
            with open(temp_file, 'w') as file_pointer:
                file_pointer.write('blahblahblah')

Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Feb 24 17:24:06 2015 -0800

    Refactored TimespanInventory.__illustrate__(). NOTE.
    
    NOTE: When creating markups using the \postscript command, avoid negative
    coordinated at all cost. LilyPond doesn't handle negative extents for markups.
    Likewise, make sure to apply a \pad-to-box command to the result of your
    \postscript command, as \postscript appears to result in a markup with a width
    and height of 0.

commit bd6bc1e42fb53d6efe1e82041a80517ee9ddfc8c
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 23 16:19:38 2015 -0700

    Added start and stop properties to BooleanPattern.
    
    Set start and/or stop to an integer to specify a range to apply the mask
    within. Setting only the start or stop to an integer creates a half-open
    interval to apply the mask within, allowing periodic masks to continue. Mask
    indices start relative to the interval's start.
    
        >>> mask = rhythmmakertools.BooleanPattern(
        ...     indices=[1, 2],
        ...     period=3,
        ...     start=1,
        ...     stop=-1,
        ...     )
        >>> total_length = 10
        >>> for i in range(11):
        ...     matches = mask._matches_index(i, total_length)
        ...     print(i, matches)
        ...
        (0, False)
        (1, False)
        (2, True)
        (3, True)
        (4, False)
        (5, True)
        (6, True)
        (7, False)
        (8, True)
        (9, False)
        (10, False)
    
    Also:
    
        >>> mask = rhythmmakertools.BooleanPattern(
        ...     indices=[0],
        ...     period=2,
        ...     start=5,
        ...     )
        >>> total_length = 7
        >>> for i in range(11):
        ...     matches = mask._matches_index(i, total_length)
        ...     print(i, matches)
        ...
        (0, False)
        (1, False)
        (2, False)
        (3, False)
        (4, False)
        (5, True)
        (6, False)
        (7, True)
        (8, False)
        (9, True)
        (10, False)

commit 39dfe506c981d091c219e3047fe4951620743710
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Mar 25 15:01:11 2015 -0400

    Extended TimeSignature with __add__ and __radd__ methods. NEW.
    
    Example: same denominator:
    
        >>> TimeSignature((3, 4)) + TimeSignature((3, 4))
        TimeSignature((6, 4))
    
    Example: different denominators:
    
        >>> TimeSignature((3, 4)) + TimeSignature((6, 8))
        TimeSignature((12, 8))
    
    Addition works the same as for nonreduced fractions.
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

commit 48f7603badc069073ff114a649879e40b16d8973
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 26 23:01:45 2015 -0400

    Extended scoretools.make_leaves() with use_multimeasure_rests. NEW.
    
    Example: without keyword:
    
        >>> scoretools.make_leaves([None], [(3, 8), (4, 8), (5, 8)])
        Selection(Rest('r4.'), Rest('r2'), Rest('r2'), Rest('r8'))
    
    Example: with keyword:
    
        >>> scoretools.make_leaves([None], [(3, 8), (4, 8), (5, 8)], use_multimeasure_rests=True)
        Selection(MultimeasureRest('R1 * 3/8'), MultimeasureRest('R1 * 1/2'), MultimeasureRest('R1 * 5/8'))
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

commit 81b930bf0d0c437d2471d1d588cbc446ee82b30f
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Mar 26 23:03:58 2015 -0400

    Integrated use_multimeasure_rests into NoteRhythmMaker. NEW.
    
    Example:
    
        mask = rhythmmakertools.SilenceMask(
            indices=[0],
            period=1,
            use_multimeasure_rests=True,
            )
        maker = rhythmmakertools.NoteRhythmMaker(
            output_masks=[mask],
            )
    
        divisions = [(4, 8), (3, 8), (4, 8), (3, 8)]
        music = maker(divisions)
        lilypond_file = rhythmmakertools.make_lilypond_file(
            music,
            divisions,
            )
    
    Result:
    
        \new RhythmicStaff {
            {
                \time 4/8
                R1 * 1/2
            }
            {
                \time 3/8
                R1 * 3/8
            }
            {
                \time 4/8
                R1 * 1/2
            }
            {
                \time 3/8
                R1 * 3/8
            }
        }
    
    See the NoteRhythmMaker API entry for this example with notation.

commit 5320de1402e09af6a0c5dd271255d5655cb9a793
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Fri Mar 27 11:29:19 2015 -0400

    Updated MeterManager.iterate_rewrite_inputs docstring. SPHINX NOTE.
    
    OLD: The docstring generated a Sphinx autosummary error.
    NEW: the docstring no longer generates a Sphinx autosummary error.
    
    Explanation: It appears that reST uses paired pipes to define substition
    targets:
    
        http://docutils.sourceforge.net/docs/ref/rst/restructuredtext.html#substitution-definitions
    
    Note that Abjad uses paired pipes to define measure boundaries with abj-style
    string input:
    
        >>> string = "abj: | 2/4 c'4 d'4 ~ |"
        >>> string += "| 4/4 d'8. r16 r8. e'16 ~ "
        >>> string += "2/3 { e'8 ~ e'8 f'8 ~ } f'4 ~ |"
        >>> string += "| 4/4 f'8 g'8 ~ g'4 a'4 ~ a'8 b'8 ~ |"
        >>> string += "| 2/4 b'4 c''4 |"
        >>> staff = scoretools.Staff(string)
    
    This means that Sphinx was erroring at every line that contains
    
        = "|
    
    ... or ...
    
        = '|
    
    ... anywhere in the line.
    
    The solution committed here is a workaround that simply replaces pipes with
    bangs:
    
        >>> string = "abj: ! 2/4 c'4 d'4 ~ !"
        >>> string += "! 4/4 d'8. r16 r8. e'16 ~ "
        >>> string += "2/3 { e'8 ~ e'8 f'8 ~ } f'4 ~ !"
        >>> string += "! 4/4 f'8 g'8 ~ g'4 a'4 ~ a'8 b'8 ~ !"
        >>> string += "! 2/4 b'4 c''4 !"
        >>> string = string.replace('!', '|')
        >>> staff = scoretools.Staff(string)
    
    Separate issue:
    
    OLD: The docstring attribute summary was mangled (ie, include markup
    characters in the attribute summary).
    NEW: The docstring attribute summary is no longer mangled.
    
    Explanation: Sphinx doesn't handle first-line docstrings that end with the
    combination of backtick followed immediately by colon:
    
        @staticmethod
        def iterate_rewrite_inputs(expr):
            r'''Iterates topmost masked logical ties, rest groups and container
            in `expr`, masked by `expr`:
    
    The solution committed here changes the final colon to a period:
    
        @staticmethod
        def iterate_rewrite_inputs(expr):
            r'''Iterates topmost masked logical ties, rest groups and container
            in `expr`, masked by `expr`.
    
    Which is the usual specification for how our first-line docstrings should
    terminate.

commit 02056058544f8305694dc69d38613928c281b357
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Sun Mar 29 20:03:46 2015 -0700

    Improved Spanner handling in Container._set_item().
    
    This commit fixes the following edge-case: given a container where the first
    child shares spanners with the container's previous sibling, or where the last
    child shares spanners with the container's next sibling, components inserted at
    the beginning or end of that container will also be properly inserted into
    those shared spanners.
    
    Consider a staff container four leaves, with the inner two leaves grouped into
    their own container:
    
        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 { d'4 e'4 } g'4")
    
    We can attach a beam to the leaves in the staff, resulting in expected output:
    
        >>> beam = Beam()
        >>> attach(beam, staff.select_leaves())
        >>> print(format(staff))
        \new Staff {
            c'4 [
            {
                d'4
                e'4
            }
            f'4 ]
        }
    
    The beam's component list also corresponds with the staff's leaves:
    
        >>> beam.components
        Selection(Note("c'4"), Note("d'4"), Note("e'4"), Note("f'4"))
    
    After inserting a component into the middle of the inner container, that
    component appears in the beam's component list:
    
        >>> rest = Rest((1, 4))
        >>> staff[1].insert(1, rest)
        >>> rest in beam.components
        True
    
    However, previous to this commit, any component inserted at the beginning or
    end of the inner container would not appear in the beam's component list:
    
        >>> chord_1 = Chord("<c' e' g'>4")
        >>> chord_2 = Chord("<d' f' a'>4")
        >>> staff[1].insert(0, chord_1)
        >>> staff[1].append(chord_2)
        >>> chord_1 in beam.components
        False
        >>> chord_2 in beam.components
        False
        >>> beam.components
        Selection(Note("c'4"), Note("d'4"), Rest("r4"), Note("e'4"), Note("f'4"))
    
    After this commit, both `chord_1` and `chord_2` appear in the beam's component
    list in the expected locations:
    
        >>> for component in beam.components:
        ...     component
        ...
        Note("c'4")
        Chord("<c' e' g'>4")
        Note("d'4")
        Rest('r4')
        Note("e'4")
        Chord("<d' f' a'>4")
        Note("f'4")
    
    All tests pass, and docs continue to build.

commit 3e6ae4aadc21427435f8627f400789bb16672006

commit fa67c54f1f130f432518cee148f820ed57273129
Author: Josiah Wolf Oberholtzer <josiah.oberholtzer@gmail.com>
Date:   Mon Mar 30 16:08:51 2015 -0700

    Adjusted TypedOrderedDict storage format specification.
    
    StorageFormatManager.get_types() makes heavy use of storage format
    specifications when it encounters a class implementing one. For instance, it
    looks at any keyword names defined for that class's storage format
    specification, and examines the associated values to determine more types to
    add to its list of encountered types. It also examines any declared positional
    argument values.
    
    TypedOrderedList declared in its storage format specification that its one and
    only positional argument value was its "_collection" value, which happens to
    always be an instance of collections.OrderedDict. *That* was why OrderedDict
    was appearing in the type list.
    
    This commit replaces "self._collection" with "list(self._collection.items())",
    preserving order but removing the unnecessary OrderedDict reference.

commit 955c1bb05046116d475794af8bd47772783e319e
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 31 10:54:06 2015 -0400

    Added previous_segment_metadata=None to SegmentMaker.__call__() method.
    
    The new signature is this:
    
        SegmentMaker.__call__(
            self,
            segment_metadata=None,
            previous_segment_metadata=None,
            )
    
    This is the first in a couple of commits that will cause the IDE to pass two
    metadata dictionaries to every segment-maker at illustration-time: one metadata
    dictionary for the current segment and a second metadata dictionary for the
    previous segment.
    
    Motivation is to allow every segment to know about end settings (like effective
    instrument, clef, tempo) of the segment that ends just before.

commit 3970cf6de830e0abd4da97e769da6d64239fc793

commit a3f5ce20db53a44bd9fe7f55fd87a262ba0e35df
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Tue Mar 31 19:30:30 2015 -0400

    Added check_conflicting_clefs() method to WellformednessManager. NOTE.
    
    Conflicting clefs is a relatively obscure situation defined equal to two
    different clefs being set on components that start at the same time in the same
    score.
    
    An exception raises and prevents composers from doing this directly.
    
    But there are relatively straight-forward cases when composers can create this
    situation without triggering the exception.
    
    NOTE: An extensive docstring is included with this commit and should be read.
    
    The check now runs automatically as part of any call to
    insepct_()is_well_formed().

    Graph attributes can now be overridden via graph().
    
    Pass a dictionary with the keyword "graph_attributes", "node_attributes" or
    "edge_attributes" to update keys in the to-be-graphed graph's attribute lists.
    
        meter = metertools.Meter((12, 8))
        graph(meter, node_attributes={'style': 'rounded'})

commit 353118e296ea848d15ab27e11f7f26f0326e34a7
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Wed Apr 1 14:39:40 2015 -0400

    Activated TieSpecifier.use_messiaen_style_ties. NEW.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> maker = rhythmmakertools.NoteRhythmMaker(
        ...     tie_specifier=rhythmmakertools.TieSpecifier(
        ...         tie_across_divisions=True,
        ...         use_messiaen_style=True,
        ...         ),
        ...     )
    
        >>> divisions = [(4, 8), (3, 8), (4, 8), (3, 8)]
        >>> music = maker(divisions)
        >>> lilypond_file = rhythmmakertools.make_lilypond_file(
        ...     music,
        ...     divisions,
        ...     )
    
    Results in:
    
        \new RhythmicStaff {
            {
                \time 4/8
                c'2
            }
            {
                \time 3/8
                c'4. \repeatTie
            }
            {
                \time 4/8
                c'2 \repeatTie
            }
            {
                \time 3/8
                c'4. \repeatTie
            }
        }
    
    See the NoteRhythmMaker API entry for an illustrated example.
    
    NEW: should be included in the 2.16 release notes.

        >>> staff = Staff("c'4 d'4 e'4 f'4")
        >>> slur = Slur()
        >>> attach(slur, staff.select_leaves())
        >>> print(format(staff))
        \new Staff {
            c'4 (
            d'4
            e'4
            f'4 )
        }
        >>> detach(slur)
        >>> print(format(staff))
        \new Staff {
            c'4
            d'4
            e'4
            f'4
        }

commit 87166d4abdf6d38d8d39a5028a2ab1bf47bbed38
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 2 15:22:51 2015 -0400

    Added is_compound property to Meter.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> for numerator in range(1, 13):
        ...     meter = metertools.Meter((numerator, 8))
        ...     string = True if meter.is_compound else ''
        ...     print(str(meter), string)
        ...
        1/8
        2/8
        3/8
        4/8
        5/8
        6/8     True
        7/8
        8/8
        9/8     True
        10/8
        11/8
        12/8    True
    
    Compound meters defined equal to those meters with a numerator divisible by 3
    (but not equal to 3).

commit 8d38eaab6f495e65472a6b5dcbc6792a8ddb9f13
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 2 15:29:19 2015 -0400

    Added is_simple property to Meter.
    
    Example:
    
        >>> for numerator in range(1, 13):
        ...     meter = metertools.Meter((numerator, 4))
        ...     string = True if meter.is_simple else ''
        ...     print(str(meter), string)
        ...
        1/4     True
        2/4     True
        3/4     True
        4/4     True
        5/4     True
        6/4
        7/4     True
        8/4     True
        9/4
        10/4    True
        11/4    True
        12/4
    
    Simple meters defined equal to those meters that are not compound.
    
    The two categories are completely complementary because beats either divide
    into two parts (simple) or else into three parts (compound).

commit 1d5bdb99475cf857a421bfe889b93086fe81e674
Author: Trevor Bača <trevorbaca@gmail.com>
Date:   Thu Apr 2 16:27:25 2015 -0400

    Implemented Meter.geat_beats(beat_duration) method. NEW.
    
    Example 1a. Gets quarter-note-durated beats of 6/8:
    
        >>> beat_duration = Duration(1, 4)
        >>> metertools.Meter((6, 8)).get_beats(beat_duration)
        [Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4), Duration(1, 4)]
    
        This interprets the meter as simple.
    
    Example 1b. Gets dotted-quarter-note-durated beats of 6/8:
    
        >>> beat_duration = Duration(3, 8)
        >>> metertools.Meter((6, 8)).get_beats(beat_duration)
        [Duration(3, 8), Duration(3, 8)]
    
        This interprets the meter as compound.
    
    The API contains many examples.
